I think why mixing them, making it purple, is because there is generally more magenta (on the red side) and blue pigments. Blue actually has the magenta pigment (the true primary colour) and same goes for red. Most dark colours use blue pigments to create the dark colour. As a result, you get to lean more onto purple.

It's purple because the pigments we use to produce red and blue colours are more concentrated than the yellow ones - which tend to be quite dilute-able to still show up on their own but then that means there's less pigment compared to red and blue products which usually come in much more varying levels of intense-ness! If you added more yellow or orange to the mix you'd start to get brown or you could add green-yellow to get a more black colour :D

Late comment, but the reason these mixes almost always turn out purple is being red and blue pigments are typically stronger than yellows, so even though there are yellow pigments going in (with the orange, yellow, and green) the reds and blues overtake those tones and what you end up with is purple with a bit of yellow that tones down the saturation of the color.

Okay, okay. So I have a weird obsession w color theory (artist + art history major), so lemme try to explain this... iI hope it makes sense!   You might think that in any given "mixing all my ____ together" the end result would be brown because of art class and the color wheel, but the ones I've seen turn out purple, like yours. This is because the volume of cyan and magenta pigment is more than yellow pigment, leaning overall toward purple the most. If all the pigments were equally used in the formulas, then it would obviously be brown. I suspect that could happen if greens, oranges, and yellows were more popular colors to paint your nails with! What is most mystifying to me is how dark the franken-holo taco was, but I assume the formulas use more black/dark blue pigment than I would expect in order to get a bold, jewel-tone look.   Aaahh, a wall of text that i don't know if anyone will see, nice :)

I think I know why mixing cosmetic items together results in purple. First, there are colors called "warm-toned" and "cool-toned". The main warm-toned colors being red, yellow, orange, and the main cool-toned colors being blue, purple, and green. In cosmetics, whether it be nail polish, make-up, etc, the colors red and blue are very popular, or colors like yellow, orange, purple, and green which are very similar to red or blue. For example, if you were to mix yellow, orange, and red together, red would most likely dominate the other warm tone colors. To create purple, you mix a warm and cool tone together, red and blue. So, if in cosmetics there are so many warm and cool tones, red and blue being the most popular, then it would make sense to get purple when mixing everything together.
